(function () {

var pageload = {
	pagemark: '451214276865625052',
	before_content: (new Date).getTime()
};
function pageload_done( $, console, maybe ){
	pageload.after_readycode	= (new Date).getTime();
	pageload.content_ready_time	= pageload.content_ready - pageload.before_content;
	pageload.script_ready_time	= pageload.after_readycode - pageload.content_ready;
	pageload.ready_time		= pageload.after_readycode - pageload.before_content;
	// Only report 1% of cases.
	maybe || (Math.random()>0.01) || $.ajax({ data: {
		op: 'page_profile',
		pagemark: pageload.pagemark,
		dom: pageload.content_ready_time,
		js: pageload.script_ready_time
	} });
}
</script>

<script type="text/javascript">
(function(){
var regexp=/\s*(?:\d+|many)\s+more\s*/i;

	
	var auto_more_count = 1;

	function auto_more(){
		var $more_link = $('#more-experiment a');
		$more_link.each(function(){
			var $lastitem = $('#firehoselist>article.fhitem:visible:last');
			if ( Bounds.intersect(window, $lastitem) ) {
			 // _any_ click can trigger, but click-specific ad will win
				setTimeout(function(){ inlineAdFirehose($lastitem, 1); }, 0);
			
				!--auto_more_count && (auto_more=undefined);
				// don't allow a call till the next paginate gets built and |more_possible|
				$(document).unbind('scroll', call_auto_more);
			}
		});
	};

	function call_auto_more(){ auto_more && auto_more(); }
	

$('#more-experiment a').
	live('more-possible', function( event ){
		var $more_link=$(this);
		if ( regexp.test($more_link.text()) ) {
		
			$(document).bind('scroll', call_auto_more);
		} else {
			$(document).unbind('scroll', call_auto_more);
		
		}
	});
})();
</script>

$(document).ready(function(){
    if(janrain) {
        $("a.janrain").live('click', function () {

            var $anchor = $(this);
            var provider = $anchor.attr("data-provider");
            var url = $anchor.attr("data-url");
            var message = $anchor.attr("data-message");
            var title = $anchor.attr("data-title");

            janrain.engage.share.reset();
            janrain.engage.share.showProvider(provider);
            janrain.engage.share.setTitle(title);
            janrain.engage.share.setMessage(message);
            janrain.engage.share.setUrl(url);
            janrain.engage.share.show();
            return false;
         });
    }
});

<script type="text/javascript">
$(function(){
var $CURRENT_MENU, $TAG_MENU=$('#tag-menu'), NOTNOT=/^!!/, IE7=/^7\.0/, TAG_PREFIX=/^\/tag\//;

function get_tag_name( $tag ){
	return ($tag.attr('href') || '').replace(TAG_PREFIX, '') || $tag.text().toLowerCase();
}

function trigger_menu( e, selector, $menu, menu_content ){
	var $target=$(original_target(e, selector)), in_use=$target.is('.trigger');
	if ( $CURRENT_MENU ) {
		$CURRENT_MENU.menu('cancel', e);
		$CURRENT_MENU = null;
	}

	if ( !in_use ) {
		menu_content && $menu.stop(true, true).hide().html(menu_content);
		($CURRENT_MENU=$menu).menu('context', e);
	}
	return !in_use;
}

function open_menu( trigger, $menu ){
	var $trigger=$(trigger), $fhitem=$trigger.closest('.fhitem');
	$fhitem.length && user_intent('interest', $fhitem[0]);

	$menu.appendTo(document.body).css({ opacity:0 }).show();

	var 	right	= $fhitem.offset().left + $fhitem.width(),
		global	= $trigger.offset(),
		local	= $menu.offsetParent().offset();

	// Ugly IE position hack required:
	$.browser.msie && IE7.test($.browser.version) && (local.top = 0);

	// pin the menu (horizontally) on-screen
	global.left = Math.min(global.left, right-$menu.width());

	$trigger.addClass('trigger');
	$menu.css({
		position:	'absolute',
		top:		global.top - local.top + $trigger.height(),
		left:		global.left - local.left,
		opacity:	1
	});
}

function close_menu( trigger, $menu ){
	$menu.hide();
	$(trigger).removeClass('trigger');
	($CURRENT_MENU===$menu) && ($CURRENT_MENU=false);
}

/* T2 tag context-menu */
var $TAG_MENU=$('#tag-menu'), NOTNOT=/^!!/;


    var user_is_admin = 0;

	

$('a[rel=tag]').live('mousedown',function(ea){
    window.open(this.href);
    return false;
})

$('.tag-bar .disagree').live('mousedown',function(ee){
	var fhitem = $(original_target(ee)).closest('.fhitem')[0],
		command = ('!' + $(original_target(ee)).attr("data-tag")).replace(NOTNOT, '');
    try { Tags.submit(fhitem, command); } catch ( err ) {  }
    return false;
})



$('a[rel=tag]').
	live('mousedown', function( e ){
        
            return true;
        

	}).
	live('click', function( e ){
		if ( !logged_in ) {
			var	target	= original_target(e),
				tag	= $(target).text();
			addfhfilter(tag);
		}
		e.preventDefault();
		return false;
	});

$TAG_MENU.menu({
	cssNamespace: 'slash',
	liveTriggers: true,
	clickDuration: 300,

	start: function( e, ui ){
		var	$tag	= $(ui.trigger),
			tag	= get_tag_name($tag),
			context	= firehose_settings && firehose_settings.viewtitle;

		// Insert the tagname into the menu items where needed.
		$TAG_MENU.find('span.var-tag').text(tag);
		$TAG_MENU.find('a.nix').attr('title','not ' + tag);
		

			// non-admins may only delete their own tags
		$TAG_MENU.find('a:[data-op="-"]').toggle($tag.is('.my'));
	

		// *tagname* in *viewtitle*
		$TAG_MENU.find('a:[data-op="="]').toggle(!!context);
		context && $TAG_MENU.find('span.var-view').text(context);

		open_menu($tag, $TAG_MENU);
	},

	select: function( e, ui ){
		var	$tag	= $(ui.trigger),
			tag	= get_tag_name($tag),
			op	= $(ui.select).attr('data-op'),
			fhitem,
			command;

		// Global for positioning other things.
		$related_trigger = $tag;

		switch ( op ) {
			case '=':
				addfhfilter(tag);
				break;

			default:
				fhitem = $tag.closest('.fhitem')[0];
				command = (op + tag).replace(NOTNOT, '');
				try { Tags.submit(fhitem, command); } catch ( err ) {  }
				break;
		}
	},

	stop: function( e, ui ){ close_menu(ui.trigger, $TAG_MENU); }
});




/* T2 feedback context-menu */



/* T2 datatype context-menu (admin-only) */






});
</script>

		<h2 class="story">
				
				
				
			<span id="title-22465724"> <a   href="//politics.slashdot.org/story/11/07/18/1951240/bill-clinton-says-paint-your-roofs-white">Bill Clinton Says 'Paint Your Roofs White'</a></span>
			
			
			<span class="comments commentcnt-22465724" >722</span>
			

                        
		</h2>
		<div class="details" id="details-22465724">
		
		Posted
		by 
	
	
		
			<a href="mailto:soulskill@slashdot.org" rel="nofollow">Soulskill</a>
		
	
	

	
	
	<time id="fhtime-22465724" datetime="on Monday July 18, 2011 @04:20PM">on Monday July 18, 2011 @04:20PM</time>
	
	
		<br>from the i'll-get-right-on-that dept.

	<div class="body" id="fhbody-22465724">

		


			<div id="text-22465724" class="p">
			<a href="http://poncacityweloveyou.com/" rel="nofollow">Hugh Pickens</a> writes <i>"Former President Bill Clinton thinks 'every black roof in New York should be white; every roof in Chicago should be white; every roof in Little Rock should be white. Every flat tar-surface roof anywhere! In most of these places <a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/business/archive/2011/07/paint-your-roofs-white/241784/">you could recover the cost of the paint and the labor in a week</a>.' Noting that Mayor Bloomberg started a <a href="http://articles.nydailynews.com/2010-10-14/local/27078055_1_cool-roof-greenhouse-gas-emissions-coating">program to hire and train young people to paint New York's roofs white</a>, Clinton says a big percentage of the kids have been able to parlay this simple work into higher-skilled training programs or energy-related retrofit jobs. The benefit: not only will 'cool roofs' lower the utility bill in every apartment house 10 to 20 percent,  but it frees cash that can be spent to increase economic growth. Clinton presented this with fourteen <a href="http://www.newsweek.com/2011/06/19/it-s-still-the-economy-stupid.print.html">additional ideas for growing the economy, saving energy, and attacking the jobs crisis</a>."</i>

			</div>

		<div id="comment_body_36805084"><p>Ah, the illusion of choice.</p><p>They're not "of their own choice" if there isn't a ready choice. If all the homes for sale of a particular kind in a particular area are all HOA, then people who don't want a HOA will end up being in one against their will.</p></div>
	</div>

		<div class="title">
			<h4><a id="comment_link_36804184" name="comment_link_36804184" href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804184" onclick="return D2.setFocusComment(36804184)" >Re:Great, so how the hell do I paint ashalt shingl</a>


		 	<span id="comment_score_36804184" class="score"> (<a href="#" onclick="getModalPrefs('modcommentlog', 'Moderation Comment Log', 36804184); return false"><span class=opt>Score:</span>5</a>, Informative)</span></h4>
		</div>
		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~Solandri">Solandri</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~Solandri">(704621)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36804184">		
		on Monday July 18, 2011 @05:19PM (<span class="ind"></span><a href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804184">#36804184</a>)
		<small> </small>
</span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36804184"><blockquote><div><p>What will white roofs do in the winter? Make the building colder?</p></div></blockquote><p>
I suspect they would actually make the building warmer.  It's a common misconception that black absorbs heat while white reflects it.  Well, that in itself isn't the misconception, the misconception is that people think of the heat transfer happening only one way.  Black is <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emissivity" title="wikipedia.org">more conducive to heat transfer</a> [wikipedia.org] than white.  That means if you have a black roof in winter (assume no snow), and the inside of the house is warmer than the outside, the black roof will radiate the interior heat to the sky faster than would a white roof.  Think of white paint as a heat insulator, and black paint as a heat conductor.
<br> <br>
True, during daylight the radiation from sunlight into the roof may exceed the radiation from inside the house to outside.  But days are short in Winter, and I suspect the heat loss during the night far exceeds the gain during the day.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentSub" id="comment_sub_36804184">

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803714"><p>1)Ridge vents can only be installed on pitched roofs.  Many large buildings do not have pitched roofs.<br>2)Painting a roof white requires no permits, construction, tools (save paintbrushes and maybe brushes/cleaning solutions), specialized skills, etc.<br>3)Titanium Dioxide, used to make many white paints white, is a photo-catalyst, which means it can self-clean and chew up pollutants in the air.<br>4)A ridge roof vent that is controllable requires control systems and whatnot.  White paint simply works.</p><p>#2 is particularly important for people with few vocational skills...and landlords who, especially in NYC, are really, really cheap assholes who view tenants as human ATMs, and who won't do anything unless there's a quick, proven payback.</p><p>Clinton's point is that white paint is cheap, easy, simple, reliable, has virtually no operational expenditure, and a quick payback. Installing ridge vents shares almost nothing in common with his solution.</p></div>
	</div>

		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~hey!">hey!</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~hey!">(33014)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36804822"></span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36804822"><p>I installed a ridgeline vent on one of my office over the garage -- totally passive, but highly effective. It wasn't too bad to install either.  You just take your circular saw and cut along the roofline on either side of the peak, then nail down the ridge vent over the long crack you've just exposed.   You need to put soffit vents in too otherwise the ridge vent won't work, but that's easy.  The natural tendency of heated air to rise means you don't need any control systems.  So a ridgeline vent is a no-br<span class="substr"> </span></p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentSub" id="comment_sub_36804822">

		<div id="comment_body_36804880"><blockquote><div><p>Ummm...I don't have a black asphalt roof on my home in Mesa, AZ. I have clay tiles.</p></div>
</blockquote><p>
IIRC, one of the reasons that traditional clay tile roofs have been around so long, particularly in warm climates, is that there is a continuous flow of air between the tiles and the underlayment due to natural convection.  The tiles may get quite hot, but the air flow keeps most of that heat from reaching the rest of the building.</p></div>

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803514"><p>I'd use white roof coating, rolled on some test shingles nailed to a sheet of plywood before trying any specific coating on a home. It may take a couple of coats to cover. I would also consider a light gray coating if available.</p><p><a href="http://www.roofcoatings.org/wcc.html" title="roofcoatings.org">http://www.roofcoatings.org/wcc.html</a> [roofcoatings.org]</p><p>The temp reduction is no joke. I coated the tops of my ISO container shop buildings and my metal house roof white. The ISOs are sealed, no windows (stormproof and keeps my gear dry) and get rather warm. White tops make them reasonable workspaces.</p><p>I didn't add the glass microspheres one can buy to mix with paints and roof coatings, but I'll do that next time. (BTW I fucking HATE asphalt shingles. If I won the lottery I'd use steel trusses and modern standing seam roofing.)</p></div>
	</div>

		<div class="title">
			<h4><a id="comment_link_36804052" name="comment_link_36804052" href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804052" onclick="return D2.setFocusComment(36804052)" >Yr doing it wrong</a>


		 	<span id="comment_score_36804052" class="score"> (<a href="#" onclick="getModalPrefs('modcommentlog', 'Moderation Comment Log', 36804052); return false"><span class=opt>Score:</span>5</a>, Informative)</span></h4>
		</div>
		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~Geoffrey.landis">Geoffrey.landis</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~Geoffrey.landis">(926948)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36804052">		
		on Monday July 18, 2011 @05:08PM (<span class="ind"></span><a href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804052">#36804052</a>)
		<small><a href="http://www.geoffreylandis.com/" title="http://www.geoffreylandis.com/" class="user_homepage_display">Homepage</a> </small>
</span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36804052"><p><div class="quote"><p>The nice disadvantage of covering a roof with solar panels is that in case of a fire barely or no water will reach the fire.</p></div><p>If your roof lets water in, yr doing it wrong.  The whole point of a roof is to <i>not</i> water through.</p><p>(The reason that the firefighters spray water on a roof in the first place is to keep old-fashioned asphalt shingles from igniting-- if the roof is fireproof, that's a feature, not a bug.  By the time the roof has burned through enough to let water into the house, it's pretty much too late to save the building.)</p></div>
	</div>

		 	<span id="comment_score_36803922" class="score"> (<a href="#" onclick="getModalPrefs('modcommentlog', 'Moderation Comment Log', 36803922); return false"><span class=opt>Score:</span>5</a>, Informative)</span></h4>
		</div>
		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~queazocotal">queazocotal</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~queazocotal">(915608)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36803922">		
		on Monday July 18, 2011 @05:00PM (<span class="ind"></span><a href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36803922">#36803922</a>)
		<small> </small>
</span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803922"><p>Well...<br>A fairly small bit of googling will get you readily assembled panels for $1.50/W. <a href="http://www.sunelec.com/solar-panels-c-5.html" title="sunelec.com">http://www.sunelec.com/solar-panels-c-5.html</a> [sunelec.com]</p><p>Admittedly, these require actually mounting on the roof, and grid-tie inverters.<br>But let's ballpark these at $3/W.<br>In sunny Scotland, I pay $.25/kWh of power.</p><p>A 1kW panel produces around 900kWh/year of electricity.<br>( <a href="http://re.jrc.ec.europa.eu/pvgis/apps4/pvest.php" title="europa.eu">http://re.jrc.ec.europa.eu/pvgis/apps4/pvest.php</a> [europa.eu])</p><p>At current prices, this 1kW panel would produce $225/year, or payback (neglecting interest!!!) in 6 years.<br>And I've just got notice that bills are going up 10%.</p><p>For 'solar laminates' - these are the bare glass panels with solar cells on which need a frame made, the cost is around $1/W, so payback can be lots sooner in some cases.</p><p>(this assumes that I can simply backfeed the meter. In the UK as it stands, you cannot do this)<br>For places with lower electricity prices, payback is questionable.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentSub" id="comment_sub_36803922">

Colorbond has a good reputation when it comes to hail, but it was over 20 years old. Solar cells had zero damage: we have both PV and hot water. In fact our insurance claim took longer because we had to wait for a solar contractor to disconnect the panels so the roofers could get underneath them. We did get a light colour for the roof, not quite white.</p><p>Oh, here in Gold Coast Australia,<span class="substr"> </span></p></div>

			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36803602"></span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803602">Three things.
<p>
One, the advantage of "painting your roof white" may depend on where you live.  Even with this sweltering heat wave, those of us living far north of the Mason Dixon line spend far less on A/C than we do on heat.  The reflective coating may not be best in every situation.
</p><p>
Secondly, it is not simply a matter of painting something white.  An optimal coating has to have a high emissivity as well as high reflectivity.  For example, a tin (galvanized metal) roof can get very hot because it is refl<span class="substr"> </span></p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentSub" id="comment_sub_36803602">

		<div class="title">
			<h4><a id="comment_link_36804120" name="comment_link_36804120" href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804120" onclick="return D2.setFocusComment(36804120)" >Re:Apologies to Mick, Keith and company</a>


		 	<span id="comment_score_36804120" class="score"> (<a href="#" onclick="getModalPrefs('modcommentlog', 'Moderation Comment Log', 36804120); return false"><span class=opt>Score:</span>4</a>)</span></h4>
		</div>
		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~Pharmboy">Pharmboy</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~Pharmboy">(216950)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36804120">		
		on Monday July 18, 2011 @05:14PM (<span class="ind"></span><a href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804120">#36804120</a>)
		<small><a href="//slashdot.org/~Pharmboy/journal/" title="Sunday August 17, 2003 @05:31PM" class="user_journal_display">Journal</a> </small>
</span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36804120"><p>A black roof doesn't help you heat a house if it is covered with white snow.  And even the south, we spend more on heating than cooling (winter is much farther from 75 degrees than summer is).  Still, heating is more a function of insulation, which isn't as effective for cooling.  Also, the angle of the sun means it is much less effective an warming in the winter.</p><p>All Clinton jokes aside, painting a black tar roof white or using a light colored shingle for a home IS a good idea, and I have recommended it for years, because the net gain in the summer is much better than the net loss in the winter.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803596"><p>Look.  Just because somebody thought of something you haven't doesn't make them dumb.  People have been talking about this for years, and *yes* they've taken into account the fact that you'd like to get solar heating from your roof in the winter.</p><p>You don't get much solar heating in the winter at the latitude of New York because the days are short and the sunlight oblique.  New York is at roughly 40 degrees of latitude, and midwinter the sun rises to less than 30 degrees of elevation off the horizon.</p><p>The argument might make sense for La Paz, Bolivia, but not New York.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803686"><p>Key to this argument is the "flat" part of the roof description.  If your roof is peaked, then your angle of incidence for sunlight can be quite different from that 30 degrees (it can be up to "30 + the roof angle", depending on the  orientation of the roof).</p><p>"flat" describes most large building roofs, but not most residential roofs.  Of course he latter are what most of the commenters on this thread are talking about.... but not what Mr. Clinton is talking about.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803846"><p><div class="quote"><p>...all roofs in New York should also be painted black in winter, because damnit, it gets cold in New York in winter.</p></div><p>During the winter, day is shorter than night, and your house is always heated to ~70F (both day and night). Hence, your roof will radiate energy for longer period (night) than it would absorb the energy (day). And black bodies radiate energy better than white ones. Conclusion is that it is better to have white roof during the winter.</p></div>
	</div>

	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36803970"><p>We live on the top floor of a small apartment building that has a flat roof, and with the landlord's permission, I painted it with aluminized roof coating at the end of last summer.  I can now definitely state that our interior temperatures are about 10 F cooler than last summer (hey, we're geeks, we measured it).  We still go above ambient, but only about 5 F instead of 15 F.  It went from intolerable (there is no A/C) to not-so-bad, and the rest of the building shares the benefit, although much less than we do.</p><p>I can't speak to how much more energy we're using during the winter because we don't see those figures and didn't think of a way to measure it (like duty cycle of the heater on our floor) in time.</p></div>
	</div>

		 	<span id="comment_score_36804224" class="score"> (<a href="#" onclick="getModalPrefs('modcommentlog', 'Moderation Comment Log', 36804224); return false"><span class=opt>Score:</span>5</a>, Informative)</span></h4>

		<div class="details">
			<span class="by"><span class="byby">by </span><a href="//slashdot.org/~SoftwareArtist">SoftwareArtist</a>  <span class="uid"><a href="//slashdot.org/~SoftwareArtist">(1472499)</a></span></a></span><span class="writes" style="display:none"> writes:</span> 
			<span class="otherdetails" id="comment_otherdetails_36804224">		
		on Monday July 18, 2011 @05:22PM (<span class="ind"></span><a href="//news.slashdot.org/comments.pl?sid=2333752&amp;cid=36804224">#36804224</a>)
		<small> </small>
</span>
		</div>
	</div>
	<div class="commentBody">
		<div id="comment_body_36804224">I think you're getting confused.  What matters most is reflectivity, <i>not</i> emissivity.  The solar spectrum is most intense in the visible part of the spectrum (no surprise - that's why our eyes evolved to be sensitive to that part of the spectrum), and white paint is much more reflective in that part of the spectrum than black paint (by definition - that's what it means to be white!).
<br> <br>
And why are you quoting the emissivity of a particular paint at 3m wavelength?  That's radio frequency.  Solar energy in that frequency range is completely negligible compared to visible.</div>
	</div>

		<div id="comment_body_36804458">And what about Albedo?... <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo" title="wikipedia.org">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo</a> [wikipedia.org]
The point of being white is because of the reflected energy vs. absorbed. Only the absorbed component needs to be emitted.</div>
	</div>
